  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f2be9e7b-4e5c-43d6-9a78-ee1279888d8c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer2188312121673838818">He’s thirty-eight. I’m twenty-three.<br/><br/>He speaks Spanish. I speak English.<br/><br/>He lives in Spain. I live in Canada.<br/><br/>He dresses in thousand-dollar suits.   <span id="freeText2188312121673838818" style="display:none">He’s thirty-eight. I’m twenty-three.<br /><br />He speaks Spanish. I speak English.<br /><br />He lives in Spain. I live in Canada.<br /><br />He dresses in thousand-dollar suits. I’m covered in tattoos.<br /><br />He’s married and has a five-year old daughter.<br /><br />I’m single and can’t commit to anyone or anything.<br /><br />Until now. Because when they say you can’t choose who you fall in love with, boy ain’t that the f*#king truth.<br /><br />***<br /><br />To a restless dreamer like Vera Miles, it sounded like the experience of a lifetime. Instead of spending her summer interning for her astronomy major, she would fly to Spain where she’d spend a few weeks teaching conversational English to businessmen and women, all while enjoying free room and board at an isolated resort. But while Vera expected to get a tan, meet new people and stuff herself with wine and paella, she never expected to fall in love.<br /><br />Mateo Casalles is unlike anyone Vera has ever known, let alone anyone she’s usually attracted to. While Vera is a pierced and tatted free spirit with a love for music and freedom, Mateo is a successful businessman from Madrid, all sharp suits and cocky Latino charm. Yet, as the weeks go on, the two grow increasingly close and their relationship changes from purely platonic to something…more.<br /><br />Something that makes Vera feel alive for the first time.<br /><br />Something that can never, ever be.<br /><br />Or so she thinks.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Have you read where sea meets sky? This is primarily about Ambers cousin but its where we meet Amber for the first time, it takes place in New Zealand<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Have you read where sea meets sky? This is primarily about Ambers cousin but its where we meet Amber for the first time, it takes place in New Zealand. :) <br /><br />Karina has another stand alone series. The first book is The Pact. If you loved Love in English you will love meeting the McGregor men throughout the 5 books in that series. They dont need to be read in order at all they are all standalone. I highly recommend :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_896918502" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/896918502" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/896918502?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=cheating">cheating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boarding-school">boarding-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=jericho-fucking-barrons">jericho-fucking-barrons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alpha-male">alpha-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=b-word-heroine">b-word-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boring-main-character">boring-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer896918502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18092035496434279861"><blockquote>
  <i>He slowly turned around. <b>“What is love? In English.”</b><br/>I raised my brows. “Love, in English, is love?”<br/>“What is it in Spanish?”<br/>I was so enthralled by his hypnotic eyes, I could barely remember. “Amore?”<br/>He shook his head ever so slightly. <b>“No. Love in Spanish is you.”</b></i>
</blockquote>I got to hand it to Mateo, when you have a successful hit line, milk it for all it's worth.<br/><br/><b>This is not a contemporary romance. It is a fairy tale, a fantasy in which adultery is not only accepted but condoned and encouraged by everyo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText18092035496434279861" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>He slowly turned around. <b>“What is love? In English.”</b><br />I raised my brows. “Love, in English, is love?”<br />“What is it in Spanish?”<br />I was so enthralled by his hypnotic eyes, I could barely remember. “Amore?”<br />He shook his head ever so slightly. <b>“No. Love in Spanish is you.”</b></i>
</blockquote>I got to hand it to Mateo, when you have a successful hit line, milk it for all it's worth.<br /><br /><b>This is not a contemporary romance. It is a fairy tale, a fantasy in which adultery is not only accepted but condoned and encouraged by everyone involved</b> (except, naturally, for the unfortunate wife and child). Were this not a book, with predictable, expected elements of falling in love, we would be reading about the sad tale of a naive, broken young woman with daddy issues who got used up and spit out by an older, wiser, manipulative sports celebrity who knew just what to say to get her to spread her legs and open her heart.<br /><br />There are certain elements of romance I dislike, but which I can appreciate when done well, adultery is one of them. <b>I do not like adultery, but I read this book knowing that there will be cheating.</b> I did not start this book thinking I would hate it, <b>I started this book with an open mind</b>, but since this is a premise I do not like, I expected certain things out of it in order for it to convince me to support the couple involved:<br /><br />I wanted it to:<br />1. Show me a well-drawn, realistic, and believable romance<br />2. Show me that there is more beyond this relationship beyond that of lust and insta-love<br />3. Show me that there is actual love involved beyond the superficial<br />4. Show me why I should condone these two<br /><br /><b>This book did none of the above</b>. It did nothing to convince me that, outside of the fairy-tale fantasy of a book, that this relationship could have existed. It was not realistic.<br /><br /><b>"Well, Khanh, why did you read a fucking romance novel if you wanted things to be realistic, then?!"</b> Because I expect SOME elements of realism in my contemporary novels. Otherwise, I would be reading Harlequins with titles like <i>THE BILLIONAIRE MMA BIKER SURGEON SHEIK'S ACCIDENTAL TWIN DAUGHTERS WITH THEIR BUNNY DOLLS</i> or something like that. I wanted this book to be <i>believable</i>, is that too much to ask?<br /><br /><u>The Setup</u>: <b>Unrealistic and improbable.</b> Vera is a 23-year old college astronomy student. She is in Spain, she is enrolled to work as an English speaker for a program that will immerse native Spanish speakers with English for several weeks. She doesn't speak a word of Spanish, and therefore runs late to the bus. When she gets to the bus, there is only one seat available. <b>The one next to darkly handsome, world-famous Mateo Casellas</b>.<br /><br />Ok, some problems with that.<br /><br />1. Why the fuck is the handsome, world-famous (think retired Spanish David Beckham who now owns several famous Spanish restaurants) Mateo SITTING ALL BY HIMSELF in a country where everyone knows who he is?!<br /><br />2. Why the fuck is Mateo in this school in the first place? <b>He speaks fluent Spanish</b>, as Vera points out herself. He wants to learn to speak better English because people look down on businessmen who can't speak English well.<br /><br />Ok, understandable, BUT there are some more problems with that.<br /><br />1. Granted, we can't see the accent within the page, but <b>Mateo speaks almost flawless English</b>. My English is pretty damn perfect, and there are but few flaws in the way Mateo speaks within the book. He lacks some pop culture words, some slangs, but otherwise, his English is wonderful. As for slangs, well, shit, a book could take care of that, don't you think? It would certainly waste less time.<br /><br />2. <b>His wife speaks fluent English</b>. Why not get her help?! Arg!<br /><br /><b>The thing about this book, is that in a realistic world, Mateo and Vera wouldn't have met in the first place, because Mateo has no need of Vera's English skilllllz!</b><br /><br /><u>Vera</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>The thing was, I didn’t do love. That wasn’t my thing. That was the reason why I didn’t date, I only got laid when I needed to blow some steam or have some fun. Love was scarier than deep space.</i>
</blockquote>Could have fooled me. Vera: <b>the troubled young woman who vows never to fall in love---only to fall in insta-lust and then love---with Mateo before 30% of the book is even through.</b> A walking cliche. A clinical psychologist's dream patient, because man, is there a lot to psychoanalyze here. Troubled childhood doesn't even begin to describe it. Vera has been doing drugs since she was barely in high school. She sleeps around, she doesn't really care about her family besides her brother, she doesn't care about anyone, or anything...and nobody really cares about her either.<br /><br /><b>The thing with Vera is she's had a string of really, really incompetent boyfriends and easy lays, none of whom ever sees beyond the superficial, none of whom ever cared about her.</b> She's only ever had really, really stupid boys. It takes a mature, wise, manipulative man like Mateo all of five minutes of DEEEEEEEEP QUESTIONING INTO HER SOUL to make her feel like she's the center of the universe. He gets her to talk about herself, her wishes, her dreams. It takes SO LITTLE effort on his part to make Vera melt into a puddle of love-goo.<blockquote>
  <i>“You are special, Estrella,” Mateo said, his eyes softening as he gazed at me.</i>
</blockquote><b>Vera is an astronomy student. Mateo starts nicknaming her "Estrella," meaning "Star" in Spanish.</b> She thinks it's the most wonderfully romantic thing EVER.<br /><br />What a disappointment. I wanted Vera to be harder to seduce.<br /><br /><u>Mateo</u>:<blockquote>
  <i>“Ugly?” Mateo said in fervent disbelief. “No. You are terribly beautiful, Vera. So beautiful that it hurts. You would outshine her like the star you are.”</i>
</blockquote>A suave Spanish lover. One who knows just what to say, what buttons to push, in order to seduce a girl. Especially one so obviously broken and damaged as the tattooed, tough, blunt, hard-spoken Vera.<br /><br />In this fairy-tale world, he falls in love, improbably so, I feel. In the real world, this could have ended in Vera's broken heart. Of course, the book is set up so that Mateo falls madly in love for Vera, but <b>were it not for the book's very obvious setup of that scenario, I would not have believed it.</b><br /><br />Mateo's romantic words to Vera are lovely, exquisite, and ever-so-rehearsed. <b>They are lines from a romance novel, a movie, the sort that Nicholas Sparks would have been proud to author.</b>They are too smooth, they are too much, they are completely unbelievable...given this man is supposed to NOT have been fluent in English, remember? <blockquote>
  <i>“You already are the other woman!” he yelled right back. His words smashed into me, blowing me to smithereens. He cupped my face in his hands. “You already are, whether you want to be or not. You’ve bewitched me, Vera. You’ve blinded me. You’ve made me forget my vows. And all you had to do was shine.”</i>
</blockquote>Spare me. <b>Mateo's lines are that of an experienced seducer, one who, for all we know, could have come to the school every few months to have an affair alone.</b> God knows it's commonly done here, since others in the group have obviously confessed to having love affairs in this "school." It's not a school, it's an expensive rendezvous point.<br /><br /><u>The Affair</u>:<blockquote>
  <i>“Well…you’re married,” I said unevenly, wishing my heart would slow the fuck down, feeling completely exposed even in the dark of night.<br />“And so are many of them.”<br />“It would be inappropriate...”<br />“How do you know? Is this inappropriate?”</i>
</blockquote><b>From the very moment that Vera and Mateo lay eyes on each other, they, well, want to lay each other.</b> I wanted a slow introduction, I wanted more depth than just insta-love and insta-lust. I didn't get that. Mateo and Vera are intensely attracted to each other, they constantly flirt, touch. Mateo is horny for Vera. Vera gets her panties wet for Mateo. That's fine! <b>There's nothing wrong with insta-lust, but it doesn't convince me that this is a relationship that has any depth beyond that.</b> And it is an affair. Mateo has been wearing a wedding ring since the beginning.<br /><br />Initially, he refuses to talk about his wife. <b>But he's still married.</b><br /><br />He insinuates a difficult relationship with his wife. <b>But he's still married.</b><br /><br />We don't know what his wife is like. She could be a bitch (she's not). Regardless of what kind of personality she has, <b>he's still married.</b><br /><br />He flirts with Vera. He's still married.<br /><br />They fuck. He's still married.<br /><br />They carry on a long-distance relationship. He's still married.<br /><br /><u>The Legacy of Adultery</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>I shook my head adamantly. “It’s wrong. I don’t want to be the other woman. I’ve seen my dad go for the other woman, I can’t put his daughter through that,” I said. “Or his wife,” I quickly added.</i>
</blockquote><b>Yes. It's wrong. And her moral dilemma lasts all of 5 seconds.</b>What hurts about Vera is that she's no stranger to cheating. I wanted this book and Vera to address the morality issue, and it doesn't do it very well. Yeah, she reminds herself that he's married, she should stay away, but then Mateo makes her tinklies tingle so much that she can't really stay away for more than an hour. It goes that way throughout the book. <b>It's wrong! I'm doing it anyway. I can't help myself.</b> The internal moral deliberations are rare, indeed.<br /><br /><b>Vera's dad cheated on her mother.</b> It turned Vera's childhood into a nightmare, it destroyed her family, it changed her personality, her life. Vera knows well the implications of adultery, and she does it anyway. Vera's boyfriend in high school cheated on her consistently. She knows how much pain that entails, to suffer while your loved one is cheating on you. She does it anyway.<br /><br />If this book wanted me to sympathize with Vera, it would have done a better job of making me feel Vera's pain, hurt, her desperation to try to stay away from Mateo. The thing is, VERA NEVER TRIES REALLY HARD AT ALL. Neither does Mateo. Their relationship didn't feel like one of love, it's one based off lust, that stays focused on lust, and we're supposed to accept the fact that they're in love without much evidence.<br /><br /><u>The Other Woman (Mateo's Wife)</u>: I don't care if she's the biggest bitch in the world, she doesn't deserve to be cheated on until their divorce and separation has been finalized. <b>We're supposed to hate The Wife because she tried to change Mateo from a playboy soccer diva to a decent husband.</b><blockquote>
  <i>"But Isabel convinced him to give it all up. To get away from the lifestyle she considered too wild.”<br />“Wild?”<br />She smirked. “Oh yes. Our players are known for being a little wild and crazy. Lots of sex and fights and drinking. Mateo was no different than the rest. And Isabel, with her Duchess grandmother and her socialite status, she didn’t want that."</i>
</blockquote>*crickets chirp*<br /><br /><b>Wait a minute, so we're supposed to hate The Wife because she wanted Mateo to be something 90% of the world's wives want of their husband?!</b> IS THAT SO FUCKING WRONG TO NOT WANT YOUR HUSBAND TO CHEAT ON YOU, TO DO DRUGS, TO PARTY, AND INSTEAD SPEND TIME WITH YOUR FAMILY? I HAD NO FUCKING IDEA. I can't say that I hate The Wife at all, and in order for me to condone this affair, I should have some reason to hate the wife, to feel that Mateo is correct in seeking love elsewhere.<br /><br />He doesn't.<br /><br /><b>This book has completely failed to convince me to support the adulterous affair of Vera and Mateo.</b> No, thank you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18092035496434279861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer817262969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15050972361161613279">"The heart is wild - isn't that what rib cages are for?"<br/><br/>I heard that quote the other day and it made me realize how much it relates to this book. Because the heart doesn't listen to reason nor does it want to be tamed. The heart is made to love and it will love whoever it fucking pleases.<br/><br/>Your heart has an open mind...and coming into this story, you should too.<br/><br/>This isn't horror.<br/><br/>This isn't scary (although love is terrifying).<br/><br/>This isn't suspenseful or paranormal.<br/><br/>This is real life.<br/><br/>Real life is about</span>
  <span id="freeText15050972361161613279" style="display:none">"The heart is wild - isn't that what rib cages are for?"<br /><br />I heard that quote the other day and it made me realize how much it relates to this book. Because the heart doesn't listen to reason nor does it want to be tamed. The heart is made to love and it will love whoever it fucking pleases.<br /><br />Your heart has an open mind...and coming into this story, you should too.<br /><br />This isn't horror.<br /><br />This isn't scary (although love is terrifying).<br /><br />This isn't suspenseful or paranormal.<br /><br />This is real life.<br /><br />Real life is about heartbreak. About finding yourself and finding others in the most inconvenient circumstances.<br /><br />It's about taking risks, taking chances, and learning to fly.<br /><br />It's about giving it all on uncertainty.<br /><br />This IS real romance.<br /><br />And because it is real, it isn't safe.<br /><br />It hurts.<br /><br />I hope you'll join Vera and Mateo's story.<br /><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_755537901" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755537901" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755537901?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755537901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5188716805980623757"><b>5 Estrella Stars!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://www.amazon.com/Love-English-Karina-Halle-ebook/dp/B00JMO9W4K/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1397999104&sr=8-1&keywords=Love%2C+in+english' rel='nofollow noopener'>LIVE-Amazon</a><br/><br/><a href='http://www.barnesandnoble.com/w/love-in-english-karina-halle/1119160103?ean=2940045818889' rel='nofollow noopener'>LIVE- B&N</a><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/860cb940-0f43-42d4-9ad1-10d0686778a3_zpsb082b3f1.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397973998i/9353098.jpg' alt=' photo 860cb940-0f43-42d4-9ad1-10d0686778a3_zpsb082b3f1.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Love is powerful. Love can pull people together and tear people apart. Love has no time limit, no regard for age, religion, race or social/economic status. Love is just love. You can’t control when you fall or who you fall in love with. Sometimes, it just happens. <br/><br/>Vera and Mateo’s story isn’t easy to read. It can be difficult for some readers to read about cheating. Especially when it’s cheating within a marriage. I guess this is a disclaimer, but I reall</span>
  <span id="freeText5188716805980623757" style="display:none"><b>5 Estrella Stars!</b><br><br><a href="http://www.amazon.com/Love-English-Karina-Halle-ebook/dp/B00JMO9W4K/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1397999104&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=Love%2C+in+english" rel="nofollow noopener">LIVE-Amazon</a><br><br><a href="http://www.barnesandnoble.com/w/love-in-english-karina-halle/1119160103?ean=2940045818889" rel="nofollow noopener">LIVE- B&amp;N</a><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/860cb940-0f43-42d4-9ad1-10d0686778a3_zpsb082b3f1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397973998i/9353098.jpg" alt=" photo 860cb940-0f43-42d4-9ad1-10d0686778a3_zpsb082b3f1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Love is powerful. Love can pull people together and tear people apart. Love has no time limit, no regard for age, religion, race or social/economic status. Love is just love. You can’t control when you fall or who you fall in love with. Sometimes, it just happens. <br><br>Vera and Mateo’s story isn’t easy to read. It can be difficult for some readers to read about cheating. Especially when it’s cheating within a marriage. I guess this is a disclaimer, but I really hope it doesn’t sway people against reading this beautifully written, emotional story. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/d6309d47-c9b5-4a7d-a6d6-f2203fddff23_zps7674a9f4.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397973998i/9353099.jpg" alt=" photo d6309d47-c9b5-4a7d-a6d6-f2203fddff23_zps7674a9f4.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Our heroine, Vera has never really been in love. She is on her way to Spain, and love is the last thing on her mind. As a twenty three year old astronomy student from Canada, she will be working with Spanish speaking men and woman looking to brush up their English skills. 4 weeks at Las Palabras and her life is changed forever. Meeting Mateo changes her life forever. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/0d863dea-c989-4dd8-b018-3d1267854e48_zps58860faf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397973998i/9353100.jpg" alt=" photo 0d863dea-c989-4dd8-b018-3d1267854e48_zps58860faf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Mateo is a thirty eight year old business man. He’s a retired pro soccer player and he is married with a small child. Mateo isn’t out to find a woman. That’s not on his mind when he goes to Las Palabras to brush up on his English. Mateo’s life has changed drastically since he got injured and married his wife. It’s like the life has been sucked out of him. He’s not the same person he once was. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“You will see. Sometimes you are stuck being the person you are and not the person you were. Or could be.”</blockquote>
</i><br> But when he meets Vera, he can’t resist her. There is something about this vibrant woman that gives him hope. Makes him feel like his old self again. Mateo and Vera start developing a friendship, slowly building into more. Both fight their feelings for so long. Especially Vera. She portrays herself as a villain, she feels terrible for falling for this married man, but she never sought out to do it. She denies her feelings for so long. But sometimes, you can’t help who you fall in love with, or how fast you fall. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“You can’t fall in love in a week.”<br><br> “You can fall in love in a second. The heart has no regard for time.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/d8ecb452-1ce7-4a0b-9f13-bc4b12fd4baf_zps8a3a812a.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397973998i/9353101.jpg" alt=" photo d8ecb452-1ce7-4a0b-9f13-bc4b12fd4baf_zps8a3a812a.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So we have a younger woman and a married older man. From two totally different worlds. Both know it is close to impossible to be together, but how can you fight something so strong? Is real true love really wrong? <br><i>
  <blockquote>“Estrella, I have never wanted anyone, anything, quite like I want you.”</blockquote>
</i> And what happens when the four weeks are over with?<br><i>
  <blockquote>“There will be nights where you will feel alone and lost, where I will feel alone and lost. When that happens, I want us both to remember this, right now. Bring our thoughts back to this room, this moment. Where we aren’t lonely. Where we both are found.”</blockquote>
</i><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/11cbc907-b809-4418-b978-88a14b2a1491_zpsd2ae10a4.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397973998i/9353102.jpg" alt=" photo 11cbc907-b809-4418-b978-88a14b2a1491_zpsd2ae10a4.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As much as I loved Mateo, strangely enough, Vera was my favorite of the characters. She was far from perfect, but she was real. And deep down a good person. She was in a complicated and difficult situation and handled it the best way she knew how. I was actually proud of her for certain choices she made down the line. She was a strong heroine who was really likable to me. Mateo was sweet, sexy and swoony. There were times I questioned him actions, but by the end, he won me over. <br><br>Karina Halle’s writing is fresh, original and full of emotion. I felt the angst, the heart ache and the pain. But there were also splashes of humor, lots of love, friendship, and beauty. <br><br>Forbidden romances are my favorite. This was one of the best contemporary romances I’ve read lately. Even though the story line was somewhat controversial, it’s a story I would highly recommend to everyone. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/5396884e-ab67-4fc4-8207-c188f979fffb_zps6231f998.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397973998i/9353103.jpg" alt=" photo 5396884e-ab67-4fc4-8207-c188f979fffb_zps6231f998.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>*ARC kindly provided by author in exchange for honest review.*</i><br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Mobile%20Uploads/dcdefe78-c4fe-4634-8cb2-81ad2861b96d_zpsdd2352cd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396765643i/9184850.jpg" alt=" photo dcdefe78-c4fe-4634-8cb2-81ad2861b96d_zpsdd2352cd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5188716805980623757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_919365531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/919365531" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/919365531?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer919365531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16287146515999362363"><b>Believe it or not, I needed like a day after reading the novel to decide the rating and how to aproach my review.</b><br/><br/>I already read some novels by Karina Halle and I really like her writing style, character designing, background research for stories, etc... <br/><br/>I really like Karina Halle as author and I definitely will read more of her works.<br/><br/>So, I hope that my rating and review about this particular novel won't mislead you about my opinion about Karina Halle's work and even my overall reading experience</span>
  <span id="freeText16287146515999362363" style="display:none"><b>Believe it or not, I needed like a day after reading the novel to decide the rating and how to aproach my review.</b><br /><br />I already read some novels by Karina Halle and I really like her writing style, character designing, background research for stories, etc... <br /><br />I really like Karina Halle as author and I definitely will read more of her works.<br /><br />So, I hope that my rating and review about this particular novel won't mislead you about my opinion about Karina Halle's work and even my overall reading experience about this book.<br /><br /><b>Okay, here we go...</b><br /><br />First, I knew so early about this incoming book and since I already knew Karina Halle's work, I didn't bother to check the synopsis of the novel. In my case, now I realize that I should.<br /><br />And no, it's not because this is a full romance novel without any paranormal stuff like in the books that I have already read by her. I like romance. I think dumb that cliché about men don't read romance. True, I haven't read as much full romance novels as I have watched full romance movies (I mean material with only romance in the story without any other stuff like sci-fi, horror, fantasy, etc...). However, I trust myself to be able to enjoy reading as such.<br /><br />I can deal with psychotic serial killers, despotic dictators, dreadful monsters, cruel supervillains, etc... <b>BUT</b> I can't deal with cheating married parents. Really, I can't deal with that, even worse if they aren't the antagonist but the romantic interest of the leading protagonist.<br /><br />Being a cheating married person is already really bad in my book, <b>BUT</b> being that and also having kids and still being cheating their spouses with a third one is totally disgusting and inexcusable. Really. There isn't any valid excuse. Go, get a divorce and then, and only then, you can go and seeing/dating/having sex with anyone you like. Since, if you still are married, you aren't respecting your spouse but even worse, you are hurting your kids' feelings. When the offsprings are already adults isn't still a good situation but at least everybody is adult now and they can discuss it as adults. However, when the children are still that, children, if some of the parents (usually the father) is having trouble with his/her spouse, first they should deal with the divorce, explain as best as possible to their kids that they will going to separate, and then, and only after that, they can go and trying to find someone to love. Yes, I understand that everybody deserves to be happy on life, but they took vows and they took the responsability to have children and giving the most happy infancy possible.<br /><br />Vera Miles (yes, like the Hitchcock's film's actress) is a truly great character. She is the leading protagonist of the novel. Her reactions and doubts through the story were the reasons to make her my anchor to keep reading the novel. She is "the other woman" but she shows a totally believable escenario of how a good girl can be ending involved in a very awful situation.<br /><br />My troubles were with Mateo Casalles. The romantic interest of Vera. He is married and he has an under-age daughter. So, reading how he didn't hesitate to engage in romantic courting with Vera was disgusting. Revolting each time. Also, there are details on his behavior that it didn't give good vibes at all. I don't know if Karina Halle plans to write any sequel to the novel but I was truly suprised that he didn't do something really awful in the story. I detected all the signals of over jealous guy with dangerous potential to become violent. Also, he seems to be a controlling man that likes to say the last word on each decision of his women. I think that his real troubles with his wife were due that certainly the wife seems to be someone totally independent person and that's why Mateo was unhappy on his marriage. And finally, I have the impression too that Mateo was unfaithful more times before knowing Vera, so, I am not sure if Mateo would remain faithful to anyone. "Dog who likes to eat eggs..."<br /><br />Also, I think that the creation of the character of Mateo was overwhelming... Handsome (no trouble in that, except cases like <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, the men in romance novels are handsome), Rich, owning a line of restaurants (some trouble since he doesn't only have money, but a LOT of money, but okay, cool), and Former Soccer Star???!!! (superficiality alert!!! superficiality alert!!!)<br /><br />I don't think that Vera would need all that to find her soulmate at some moment of her life. Sure, I understand that it's a novel and women like to dream about the perfect man. Let's try the opposite case... if you would read about a young adult guy falling in love with a woman, fifteen years older than him, attractive, rich and also a former super model... would you believe that it's true honest love? I don't know, maybe I lost the point. But honestly, I don't think that you would need all that to find your soulmate. I know that I didn't at least.<br /><br />There are some really good secondary characters, some seem to be kinda jerks but they say relevant things that they need to be said, definitely in the wrong way for the wrong reasons, but at the end, they need to be said. Others are just jerks. There are some real good friends and allies. And some characters are just fillers.<br /><br />Trying to close the review. The book is very good written. Karina Halle is such gifted writer. Read the synopsis of the novel. And if you don't have any trouble with romantic stories starting in an adultery status, then maybe this is just your book. <br /><br />Honestly, I don't intend to affect the sales of the novel.<br /><br />And I know that I still want to keep reading Karina Halle's works.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16287146515999362363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_781555695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/781555695" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/781555695?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer781555695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2238899852819779464">I should probably mention that I love Karina Halle. I think she's a classy, kickass lady who has had to deal with a large amount of internet trolls, but has always remained kind and respectful to all her readers. Second, I should say that I love the way she creates flawed, realistic and slightly unlikable characters but makes you love them anyway. I was <b>addicted</b> to her <i>Sins & Needles</i> trilogy, to the point where I obsessively watched out for the release dates. And I will still buy everything Hall</span>
  <span id="freeText2238899852819779464" style="display:none">I should probably mention that I love Karina Halle. I think she's a classy, kickass lady who has had to deal with a large amount of internet trolls, but has always remained kind and respectful to all her readers. Second, I should say that I love the way she creates flawed, realistic and slightly unlikable characters but makes you love them anyway. I was <b>addicted</b> to her <i>Sins &amp; Needles</i> trilogy, to the point where I obsessively watched out for the release dates. And I will still buy everything Halle writes. I want you to know all of this before I get on to the actual review.<br /><br /><u>Because this book just didn't work for me.</u><br /><br />Or the majority of it didn't, anyway. It was one of those books that I was holding out for, trying to reach the point where I would fall in love and become absorbed in the story and the characters' lives, but that point never came. The chemistry and magic just wasn't there. It started with a main character that didn't steal my heart like Halle's other characters have, and then it just got worse the more I read. When we got to the cheating, I just didn't care anymore. Not even because I despise cheating - which I do - but because of the ridiculous, unbelievable way it was handled.<br /><br />Normally, I would describe Halle's books as anything but formulaic. That's why she appeals to me from a genre that I often have nothing but disdain for. Romance is almost always formulaic, cliched and recycled. The characters are the same people with different names and the deja angst just about kills me. Not with Halle. Not usually. Because she isn't afraid to push the boundaries of likability with morally questionable characters (but not in the typical douchey bad boy way) and she loves grit and sarcasm (like all the best people do). But that is where this book goes wrong.<br /><br />The main character is Vera. She's your regular, boring romance heroine with standard issues. She falls in instaobsession with a married dude called Mateo. He's a super rich and super pretty-faced and super boring piece of perfection. Where have I seen this before? Oh yes, in <b>EVERY SINGLE ROMANCE NOVEL.</b> <br /><br />Quite frankly, I found Mateo to be a creepy creep of Creepsville. He doesn't speak very good English, apparently, except that he does. A few words are thrown in that he doesn't understand, so the reader can see that he is such a bad English speaker... but then the rest of the time he appears to be fluent. Plus, he calls Vera "Estrella", which is Spanish for "star". I risk sounding like a thirteen year old for saying this... but <b>EWWW.</b><br /><br /><u>Then there's the cheating.</u><br /><br />You have to be seriously careful when you include cheating in romance books. It has to be handled sensitively and you have to be able to understand the characters, even if you never fully agree with what they do. But that never happens here. Vera didn't convince me that her daddy issues were a good enough excuse for her actions. The poor characterisation of Mateo's wife just left me feeling annoyed at Vera and Mateo, rather than sympathetic towards their relationship. <br /><br /><b>This book was a failed attempt at trying to turn cheaters into characters we love and care about.</b> I felt nothing for them from start to finish.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.leafmarks.com/emilymay" rel="nofollow noopener">Leafmarks</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2238899852819779464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_755520117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755520117" />
    <a title="Lucia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia"><img alt="Lucia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484242793p2/8837962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755520117?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucia" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia">Lucia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755520117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13383877932067660054">My Vera and Mateo:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398085386i/9365484._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"My name is Vera Miles.<br/>And in the story of my life, I am the villain.<br/>But I’m starting to think that most villains aren’t evil – they are just misunderstood.<br/>Or victims of that most manipulative force: love. "</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>We don't choose love. Love choses us, attacks us, surprises us when we least expect it. You cannot ignore love, you cannot simply turn your back on love when it comes to your life. Vera Miles knows it the best and this is her story to tell. Don't judge, read it. Just rem</b></span>
  <span id="freeText13383877932067660054" style="display:none">My Vera and Mateo:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398085386i/9365484._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>"My name is Vera Miles.<br>And in the story of my life, I am the villain.<br>But I’m starting to think that most villains aren’t evil – they are just misunderstood.<br>Or victims of that most manipulative force: love. "</i>
</blockquote><br><b>We don't choose love. Love choses us, attacks us, surprises us when we least expect it. You cannot ignore love, you cannot simply turn your back on love when it comes to your life. Vera Miles knows it the best and this is her story to tell. Don't judge, read it. Just remember that nothing comes without consequences or sacrifice...</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398085386i/9365485._SY540_.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Even within otherwise worn out genre of contemporary romance, Karina Halle was able to come up with new, fresh and engaging background story. English language practicing camp for adults where bunch of strangers lived together in Spanish countryside like a family was a great set up for intense interactions and funny situations. Add forbidden love, slow burn romance, thoughtfully written characters and you get this powerful story that will stay with me forever. <br><blockquote>
  <i>"Love was scarier than deep space."</i>
</blockquote><br>Love, In English is realistic and beautifully emotional love story. It is a character-driven book that made Ms. Halle’s writing style stand out and shine.This book will make you feel everything from laughing, swooning and lusting, to being depressed, anxious and on the verge of panic attack. <b>Karina Halle played with my emotions like a master puppeteer in this novel. It was, without the doubt, my best reading experience of this year.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398085386i/9365486._SY540_.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>For some poeple, subject matter may be a taboo topic. Married guy with kid and young college student? Karina Halle mastered it tastefully. Vera was strugling with her feelings, resisting, never shamelessly going for Mateo. No matter how much she wanted him. Did I see her as villain, as a bad person? Never. She was just a human being who found herself in a tricky life situation. Same goes for Mateo. He was just a loving, passionate man looking for real hapiness in his life, trying not to hurt anyone in the process. I cannot fault him for that.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“Love is like a thief, it robs you of all thought and logic and all you have left is a heart that you can only pray is strong enough to survive the rest.” </i>
</blockquote><br>Age difference, different life-style, appearence... At first sight, Vera and Mateo seem like the biggest possible opposites. But when I got to know them better, got to know their fears, dreams and passions; it was clear that they would be a perfect fit. Plus chemistry between those two was off the charts! Gradually, I found myself falling in love not only with Vera and Mateo as individual characters, but also with them as a "couple". By the end of the book I was so strongly connected with both of them, that it felt like I was right there in the story, experiencing all feelings, hopes and heartbreaks alongside Vera and Mateo. And that is exactly how a great love story should make you feel like.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398085386i/9365487.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Do not hesitate to pick this book up when it is out. I cannot recommend it enough!</b><br><br><i>*ARC provided by author as an exchange for honest review*</i><br><br>MORE REVIEWS ON MY BLOG <a href="http://readingismybreathing.blogspot.cz/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Reading Is My Breathing</b>
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13383877932067660054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer816778903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10556757713137526602"><a href='http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/HaleLoveinEnglish1TitebySueBee_zpsa37d7ee5.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“You and I, we were always a memory in the making.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>

</a><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIFS%20for%20my%20reads/LIE1storyxBbysb_zpsfc5d3487.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407767931ra/10762752.gif" alt=" photo LIE1storyxBbysb_zpsfc5d3487.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>★★★★★! Love, in English, book 1 of 2. Sometimes the heart falls in love despite your better judgment! An against-all-odds romance!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“You and I, we were always a memory in the making.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><u>Books should be read in order:</u><br><b>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/816778903" rel="nofollow noopener">Love, in English</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1021685171" rel="nofollow noopener">Love, in Spanish</a></b><br><br><b>Love, in English</b> (book 1) introduces us to astronomy student, <b>Vera Miles, Estrella</b> as she is heading to Madrid, Spain to spend a month <b>teaching English to business executives at a remote resort</b>. On the bus she meets ex-soccer star and restaurateur <b>Mateo Casalles</b> and a friendship is formed.<br><br>They are <b>polar opposites</b>, with a significant <b>age gap,</b> from <b>different continents</b>, the odds stacked against them. But more importantly <b>Mateo is married</b>, albeit unhappily so, and has a young daughter. Despite their better judgment a platonic, but intense <b>romance slowly build</b> during their month together offering tantalizing <b>sexual tension</b> until they succumb to their desires. When their time is up they must <b>return to their lives and face decisions</b> whether this is something they can or even should pursue. <br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“The heart has no regards for what’s right or wrong.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>The story goes go onto <b>follow them in the aftermath</b> of their brief affair – a bumpy road ahead as Mateo and Vera must deal with <b>guilt, demons</b> from their pasts, their <b>current situations</b> and also do some <b>soul searching</b>. Add to that the opinions and prejudices around them and you have a <b>roller-coaster of events and emotions</b>… keeping us guessing until the very last page.<br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIFS%20for%20my%20reads/LIE1HxBSbysb_zpscc5b374a.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407829608ra/10769689.gif" alt=" photo LIE1HxBSbysb_zpscc5b374a.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Seven words to describe <b> Mateo Casalles: Charismatic, reflective, lovable, respectful, possessive, private and commanding</b>.<br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIFS%20for%20my%20reads/LIE1hexBSbysb_zps0f12d90a.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407829608ra/10769690.gif" alt=" photo LIE1hexBSbysb_zps0f12d90a.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Seven words to describe <b> Vera Miles, Estrella: Sweet, insecure, smart, reflective, self-destructive, indecisive and broken</b>.<br><br><b>Love, in English</b> was to me a very <b>realistic glimpse into the ups and down of an affair</b>. Story left Mateo and Vera in a <b>good place</b>, but I couldn’t help wishing for an epilogue further into the future. Imagine my joy at discovering that a <b>second book has been announced</b> later this fall. I look forward to Mateo’s POV in book 2, <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1021685171" rel="nofollow noopener">Love, in Spanish</a>
</b>.<br><br><b>Controversial</b> plot! <b>Excellent</b> story-telling! <b>Sexy</b> and <b>oh so sweet</b> hero, Mateo Casalles! <b>Realistic</b> and <b>lovable</b> characters throughout! <br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“I would have found you. You burn too brightly to be missed.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>***<br>Hero rating: 5 stars <br>Heroine rating: 4 stars<br>Sexual tension rating: 5 stars<br>Sex scenes rating: 4.5 stars<br>Sex scenes frequency: 4 stars<br>Plot rating: 5 stars<br>Dialogue rating: 5 stars<br>Storytelling rating: 5 stars<br>Story ending rating: 4.5 stars<br>Book editing rating (5 = no edits spotted): 5 stars<br>************************************************<br><b>Overall rating: 5 stars<br><br>Would I recommend this book: Yes.<br>Would I re-read this book: Maybe later.<br>Would I read future books by this author: Yes.</b></span>

<div id="review_755934711" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755934711" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13247178-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473718933p2/13247178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755934711?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/13247178-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=arc-or-netgalley">arc-or-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=emotional-rollercoaster">emotional-rollercoaster</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755934711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5536432479057683625"><br/>★★★★★ <b>5 Brightly Shining stars!</b> ** Love, in English is now <b>LIVE</b> on <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Love-English-Karina-Halle-ebook/dp/B00JMO9W4K/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1397993203&sr=1-1&keywords=love+in+english' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397478499i/9280671.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"You are my star. You are my <b>Estrella</b>."</i>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397478687ra/9280688.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I should start of by saying that I am a huge fan of Karina Halle's work. She never disappoints. Still, I was a bit nervous about starting this book. Mainly because of the angst and emotions I thought it would evoke and the slightly taboo subject matter. Of course I should have known better; there was no need to worry because once again Karina delivers an absolute winner. This time</span>
  <span id="freeText5536432479057683625" style="display:none"><br>★★★★★ <b>5 Brightly Shining stars!</b> ** Love, in English is now <b>LIVE</b> on <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Love-English-Karina-Halle-ebook/dp/B00JMO9W4K/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1397993203&amp;sr=1-1&amp;keywords=love+in+english" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397478499i/9280671.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>"You are my star. You are my <b>Estrella</b>."</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397478687ra/9280688.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I should start of by saying that I am a huge fan of Karina Halle's work. She never disappoints. Still, I was a bit nervous about starting this book. Mainly because of the angst and emotions I thought it would evoke and the slightly taboo subject matter. Of course I should have known better; there was no need to worry because once again Karina delivers an absolute winner. This time it's not a horror or action-based story but a pure contemporary romance novel with a forbidden love element, but it was no less gripping or captivating than any of her previous work.<br><br><i>Love, in English</i> is a wonderfully crafted, thought provoking, exhilarating read with endearingly flawed characters, a strong plot and a refreshing setting. It's a story about true love and what people are willing to sacrifice in order to hold on to it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"What is love? In English."<br><b>"Love, in English, is love.</b> What is it in Spanish?"<br><b>"Love in Spanish is you."</b></i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397478499i/9280672._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"My name is Vera Miles.<br>And in the story of my life, I am the villain."</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Vera Miles</b> is a 23 year old Canadian astrology student. With her pierced, tattooed up body and her playful, adventurous personality she often manages to capture the attention of the wrong kind of crowds. They think she's a beauty with no brains, but there's so much more to her than what meets the eye. When she decides to take on a job teaching adult Spaniards English, all she wanted was to take on an adventure, see new places and meet new people. Little did she know that one month spent in Spain, would turn out to be such a life-changing experience.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397478499i/9280673._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Sometimes you are stuck being the person you are and not the person you were. Or could be."</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Mateo Cassales</b> is a 38 year old Spanish ex-soccer player, businessman and father to a 5 year old girl. He's also married, but not happily. He's charming, charismatic and breathtakingly handsome but his married status makes him strictly off limits. Still, he and Vera immediately hit it off on the bus ride to the resort where the language course takes place and as the days pass, the two of them get to know each other on a much deeper level. <br><br>When she tells him about astrology and her passion for stars, a new world opens up for him in which he wants to start over and create his own new universe. Preferably with Vera as the center of it. He's drawn to her and her unique view of life. He's never met anyone like her and he's enraptured by her beauty, both inside and out. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i><b>"You keep saying we are impossible,"</b> he said. <b>"But you don't have enough faith. You have faith in the stars, but not in us."</b></i>
</blockquote><br>Vera and Mateo's story is one with many bumps along the road. Their connection hits fast but their love grows slowly and delicately. When you chose love you would think it's not possible to make a bad decision, but what happens when that love has the power to disrupt families and break other people's hearts? This book deals with those issues in a very realistic way and it manages to make all the characters involved come out in a better way. Whether that means there's a HEA for the two main characters I will let you find out for yourself. Some readers might be put off with the age difference or the fact that the male lead is a married man, but in my experience, those elements never bothered me and they did not make the story any less enjoyable or the characters any less likeable. <br><br>While reading this book, I was right along with Vera and Mateo on the roller coaster ride of emotions they went on and once it was over, I did not want to let them go. They are not perfect characters. They make mistakes but what made them so easy to like is that they both owned up those mistakes and tried to make them right. Overall, this story is one that will definitely stay with me and that from now on resides on my all time favorites list. I would highly recommend giving it a try! ♥<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I was Vera Miles.<br>And I might have been the villain of my own story.<br>But I was the hero, too. <br>I was going to be okay."</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397479974i/9280806.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Always and infinity.</b>
</blockquote><br><b>Release date:</b> 20 April 2014.<br><br><i>**ARC kindly provided by author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4785031.Karina_Halle" title="Karina Halle" rel="nofollow noopener">Karina Halle</a> in exchange for an honest review**</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5536432479057683625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_756110889" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756110889" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/756110889?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756110889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6972030422138159484"><br/><b>*3.5 Stars*<br/><br/>Karina Halle does complicated love, and does it <i>well</i></b>.<br/><br/>A married family man with a child, plus a growing attraction for another woman has despair, destruction, and heartache written all over it. <br/><br/><b>And yet, it worked. </b><br/><br/>That's not to say this particular journey of infidelity was easy, but it was softened with <i>just</i> enough moral reasoning to be deemed acceptable, all while retaining its excitingly dangerous edge. <br/><br/><i>Love, in English</i> offers a daring yet sweet contradiction, and thoroughly showcase</span>
  <span id="freeText6972030422138159484" style="display:none"><br><b>*3.5 Stars*<br><br>Karina Halle does complicated love, and does it <i>well</i></b>.<br><br>A married family man with a child, plus a growing attraction for another woman has despair, destruction, and heartache written all over it. <br><br><b>And yet, it worked. </b><br><br>That's not to say this particular journey of infidelity was easy, but it was softened with <i>just</i> enough moral reasoning to be deemed acceptable, all while retaining its excitingly dangerous edge. <br><br><i>Love, in English</i> offers a daring yet sweet contradiction, and thoroughly showcases how the heart knows neither time nor bounds. The plot wasn't over-the-top or saturated with angst, but instead displayed a very life-like, forbidden reality of a couple who--to put it simply--couldn't help but fall in love. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I'm starting to think that most villains aren't evil—they are just misunderstood. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><b>Vera</b> is on her way to Spain, partaking in a four week program where she'll help Spanish speaking business men and women brush up on their conversational English skills. Her entire stay is paid for and Vera hopes to gain a unique experience in the process. <br><br><b>But what she encounters is more than she could have imagined...</b><br><br><b>Mateo</b> is a sexy former soccer star turned business owner, and happens to be one of the members Vera will "tutor" on her trip. Mateo appears to be a confident man who has it all together, but underneath his easy going persona lies a dejected soul who has lost himself somewhere along the way. <br><br>Vera, with her tattoos and headstrong personality represents all that Mateo used to love about life. When an immediate attraction blossoms into something much more, Mateo is faced with remaining in a loveless marriage, or following his heart. However, Mateo's daughter means the world to him; a world he simply will not stand to lose. <br><br>This story is separated into three parts, and I was especially fond of the first. It had all the typical KH ingredients: humor, sex appeal, tension, witty characters, and, of course, a spark that set off one hell of an unpredictable romance. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>You can tell me to stop and I will stop. But please don't tell me to stop.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> <br><b>On the subject of adultery, because it's not an easy pill to swallow even in fiction: </b>This issue was handled tactfully, never giving me that icky, <i>terrible, horrible, no good, very bad</i> feeling. Vera suffers insurmountable guilt and is in a constant state of fighting her "inappropriate" feelings for Mateo. She was a conscientious heroine placed in a difficult, hard-to-ignore situation, and I never found myself struggling to accept her behavior. <br><br>All of that said, I was hoping for a bit more in the wrap up, which is strange because the story is over five hundred pages long. Certain elements felt slightly rushed, but I guess it had to end sometime. <b>Good read!</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Promise me, you won't give up on us...<br>I won't, I said, though not out loud. I was too afraid to say it, in case it didn't end up being true. </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>
</b><br><b>▪	 Genre/Category:</b> Contemporary Romance<br><b>▪	 Steam Caliber:</b> Very steamy<br><b>▪ Romance:</b> Forbidden elements. Complicated and intense. <br><b>▪	 Characters:</b> Strong, yet unsure heroine. Sexy, distinguished, but dejected hero.<br><b>▪	 Plot:</b> A married man and single woman find love. Forbidden elements. <br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Witty, humorous, and fluid. <br><b>▪ POV:</b> 1st Person: Heroine<br><b>▪	 Cliffhanger:</b> None/Standalone <br><b>▪ HEA? </b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><i>*Many thanks to author for mailing copy of arc in exchange for an honest review*</i><br><a href="http://s293.photobucket.com/user/kfuller5_2008/media/534b3dcd-c5b6-4f95-85f1-c4bc5520e697_zps0874debe.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="270" width="190" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396638666i/9164391._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 534b3dcd-c5b6-4f95-85f1-c4bc5520e697_zps0874debe.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><a href="http://prettywordsbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412050368i/11316768.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Pretty-Words-Book-Blog/860331017317983" rel="nofollow noopener">
